1. It js requested that the Operational Approval for
LINUFF-2 be cancelled.

2. While the Station continues to receive copies of
LIHUFF-2 publications and veports through LINUFP-1, the Station
no longer gives financial support nor dixéction to’ LIHUFF-2's
efforts. The Station receives all information from LIHUFF-2
indirectly through LINUFF-1; there is no direct contact. The
Station gives no direction or requ. aents to LINUFF-2, and
merely accepts what LIWUFF-1 passes on.

acres

3. In view of the above, the Station feels there is’ no
need to retain LIHUFP-2's OA. Subject is mded for
recontact, but anyone contacting LINUFF-2 should be avare
that this asset is extrenely biased aud right-wing, and is in
dire need of financial backing for his pro-U.S. and pro-

private capital investment magazine, Espejo. f

(\ MHSPAWN/Forwarding Book on Revolutioy
| ACTION REQUIRED - REFERENCES. ar

Action Required: FYI

1, Attached is a book on revolutionary theory, "La Iglesia,
el Subdesarrollo y la Revolucion," recently published by
"Editorial Nuestro Tiempo" (which often publishes pro-Communist
material), which was brought to the Station's attention by
,LIHUFF-1 on 22 October 1968.

2. With the exception of one of the ten authors who
contributed to this book (Karl LENKERSDORF) all others subscribe,
in one way or another, to the developing thesis that Christian
(both Catholic and Protestant) theology justifies the use of
violence (i.e., killing if necessary) to bring about basic
structural changes in the "Third World." An undercurrent of
sympathy for revolutionary "martyrs" "Che" Guevara and Camilo
Torres permeates uost of the writings, as does the old favorite
shibboleth of Latin American "intellectuals" that the United
States has purposely kept Latin America underdeveloped (to
maintain a source of cheap raw materials and a market for
expensive manufactured goods).

Remove fron Project KOACEfewve.
CS Ciazsifisation: SOM YROS

6 November 1968

HAIMA-35792

SECRET 200~1 24-162

1

meting achithLichstes


Coneee CATION [otra iem Sewooe AND NUETA
SECRET HMMA-35792

CONTINUATION OF
= DISPATCH

3. Ina strange marriage of "progressive" Catholic philosophy
with the old positivistic liberai tradition (which, by the way, was
quite anti-Catholic up to the days of the Mexican Revolution), this
pook addresses itself to well-documented statistical studies (mostly
produced under United Nations auspices) to state the case of Latin
American underdevelopment, and then proceeds to justify violent
revolution with Cnristian principles on the grounds that basic
needs for human subsistence have, been denied to the Latin American s
masses. The Thomistic principle.-that he who is starving may kill (yee
to get food is f¥cqtichtly auotéd; but no effort is made to define © #*
“basic needs" i1 the modern world (obviously, millions of Latin af
Americans are not starving to death; and there is little agreement
on what constitutes "subsistence level"). Therefore, without
defining what are “indispensable needs," most of the authors agree
that basic structural changes are required to satisfy these
(undefined) needs, and proceed to the next step: this justifies
violent revolution.

4. The problem is that most of the authors depart from a
basically Marxist-positivist point of view: the assumption that
private enterprise is incompatible with social justice, and that
only a fundamentally socialistic economy can provide the infra-
structure for an equitable distribution of wealth.

5. Despite the verbosity of the writers, their message is
simple: (A) statistical analyses show two-thirds of the world is
starving and lacks "basic needs of human existence;" (B) history
shows that "The Establishment" will not give in to reason; oa
(C) divine natural law stipulates that man has an overriding right
to satisfy his basic needs; (D) since "The Establishment" will not
give in to reason, divine natural law authorizes violent revolution
to establish an “equitable distribution of wealth." But what
system would follow violent revolution to insure equitable distri-
bution? The Marxist bias of the authors comes forth. Tomas G.
ALLAZ, French Dominican priest who teaches at the Seminario de
Leon, Gto., Mexico, frankly quotes with approval a famous passage
from "L'Osservatore Romano" of 8 May 1949: "Communism as such, '
that is, as an economic system, leaving aside its philosophy, is
not against the very nature of Christianism as much as, is
capitalism." In another passage, Father ALLAZ also exemplifies
the authors’ anti-U.S. bias: “Children in Vietnam are cut to
pieces by the bombs of the Good Samaritans of the world.”
Communist terror is nowhere mentioned. The book, therefore,
appears to be essentially an effort to justify with Christian
theology Fidel CASTRO's call to arms against the status quo in * :
Latin America. 7

6. Index book authors, "Che" Guevara, and Camilo Torres.

for/Willard C. CURTIS

Attached hereto ia a full-page spread which appeared in
"Excelsior" of Hexico City on 6 August 1968, It is a paid ad
signed by Vicente Lombardo Toledano and the Partido Popular
Socialista (PPS) attacking the FBI and CIA (especially tho
latter) for their alloged conspiratorial interference in Hexican
affairs. This is one more rather feeble leftist attempt to
involve U.S. agencies in tke recent student disturbances, Note
that among other charges, the CIA is alleged to be supporting
the right-wing student organization, NURO.

LIHUFF Progress Report/ 1 July 1967 through 31 Nay 1968

FacTion RTQUIRED. REFERERS

HMMA~34773
HMNA~-34757

REFERENCE: A.

1. During the past year the main activities of this project
(which consists of only LIHUFF/1, a WOLADY citizen contract agent)
have been aimed at:

Saas

a) Procuring reports on right wing political groups and
right-wing student organizations. These data are obtained by
LIHUFF/1 from LICHANT/1 and LIHUFF/2, both of whom are non-
paid contacts of LIHUFF/1.

b) The use of M.U.R.O, extreme right wing Catholic
student organization, principally at tae Universidad Nacional;
Autonoma de Mexico (UNAM), with branches in several provincial
univerisities.

c) The use of LIHUFF/1 to make (business) organization
traces through Dun and Bradstreet and similar groups. LIHUFF/1
and his organization (through LIHUFF/1) are also used to
procure background, operational and investigative data needed
by the Station,

2. EFFECTIVENESS:

Some examples of the work done by LIHUFF/1 are cited below:

a) Some forty (40) Dun and Bradstreet reports were
obtained during the period on individuals and/or organizations ;
of interest to this Station. *

i

b) During this period LIHUFF/1 provided the Station :
with details of Mexican Government plans to impose legisla—
tive restrictions on foreign investments and of Mexican
Government orders to Mexican Banks to limit loans to private
corporations with an appreciable amount of foreign capital.
(Note: This proved of particular interest to the Embassy).

SUSE HUFF Progress Report | July through 31 October 1966

"ACTION FEQUIRED - REFERENCES

Reference: HMMW-14683 dated 24 June 1966

i 1, The LIHUFF project was last approved on 18 June 1966 for
the period 1 July 1966 through 30 June 1967 for a budget of U.S.
dollars $4,200.00. This project provides the Chief of Station Mexico
with a source (LIHUFF-1) who has access to right-wing organizations
in Mexico, including a student action group at the Universidad
Nacional Autonoma de Mexico (UNAM) known as Movimiento Universitario

de Renovadora Orientacion (MURO).

2. Summary of Project Activit

a. This project provided the Station with a copy of
a manuscript of the first half of a book on communism written by
Father Baldomero OROTONEDA Comas, a Jesuit priest assigned to
this task by his order. Though the reviewing officers at the
Mexico Station felt that the manuscript contained no information t
useful for the Station's operational program, a microfilm was i
transmitted to Headquarters for more detailed review and recom= i

pastaoeisotsctonssosss

mendations (HMMA-29365 dated 5 July 1966).

b. During this reporting period, LIHUFF-1 reported
regularly on the situation at the UNAM and while this information
did not result in positive intelligence disseminations, it was

useful for background purposes.

c. During July 1966 the LIHUFF student organization,

with the help of Senator Alfonso GUERRA of Nayarit, initiated a
press campaign against the Czech Embassy and the Commercial Office
in Mexico, singling out for attack Emil HRADECKY (201-204658),

ATION REQUWED RFE RERES

REFERENCE: EMM-10,841, 16 November 1966

1. Referenced report, entitled "Crigins of the Student
Disturbances at the University of Hichoocan, Morelia, Michoacan",
included a statement in field comment number 11 to the effect that
Someone had caused to be published in the 10 November 1966 issue of
El Universal an article exposing the Central Racional de Estudiontes
Democraticos (CNED) of being nothing more than a dependency of the
Mexican Communist Party @ci), A coment on the cover skeet to that
report stated that a member of the HURO, using a faked PCH carpet,
had caused the arti-le to be published. :

2. The Station now knows from the LITEMPOs and LINUFF~1 that a
MURO member did, in fact, go to the offices of El Universal and using
his faked PCH carnet Plunked down the necessary money (approxinately.
21,150 MN) and had the article printed. The purpose of the operation
Was to try to discredtt the CNED just prior to its nationel meeting
held in Monterrey on 17, 18 nnd 19 Novenber 1966. While most People
in the PCH, the CNED and other organizations controlled by, or *
affiliated with the PCM are aware that the PCM controls the CNED,
many of the organizations and members of the CNED in the interior of
the country and the Nexican Public in general are not aware of PCH
control and influence in the CED,

3. Although there is no indication that the article had any
adverse effect on the CNED meeting in Monterrey, it is clear that the F
was disturbed about it and took steps to bring action against E1
Universal, accusing this newspaper formally of trying to damage the
reputation of the PCH and the CNED. ia Voz de Mexico, issue number
1857, 20 November 1866, carried an artic. € on the front page which
stated that on 17 November 1966 Arnoldo MARTINEZ Verdugo, First
Secretary of the PCM, made a formal accusation against El Universal
to the Attorney-General of the Republic, and it added that tis.
hoped that the authorities will take the appropriate action",

d. At the UNAM School of Philosophy and Letters there
opened a Chinese Communist Art Exhibit in August 1966. With the
concurrence of Chief LNPURE and in response to a request by
another LNPURE official, the Chief of Station contacted LIHUFF-1
and proposed .a harassment activity against the exhibit. On
26 August 1966 LIHUFF-1 reported that the LIHUFF student group
had been successful in their harassment attempts and the art items
were hurriedly removed. This was confirmed by the official of
LNPURE concerned, who, as well as Chief LNPURE, was Pleased with

the success of the student group, (HMMA-29922 dated 3] August
1966 reported on the above.)

e. The other successful harassment activity organized
by the LIKUFF student group took place on 23 October 1966. This
was @ student demonstration in front of the Soviet Embassy and
in front of the Cuban Embassy of approximately 200 members with
Placards, a coffin, and various banners Protesting Soviet brutality
on the 10th anniversary of the Hungarian Rebellion. (See HMMA- 3
30426 for details and Press clippings, ) nea

3. Agent Contact, ‘

approximately every week depending upon the need. No other Station
personnel are in contact with this agent nor is the Chief of
Station, Mexico, in contact with members of the LIHUFF student group,

against his 1964 income tax payment. This was turned over to the | |

1, Reference A is incorrectly titled. There is no “"LIHUFF
Student Subsidy" -- and the payments given to this group were and
are for specific jobs done at Station {and in one case at Chief
LNPURE) specific request.

2, Station requests for specific actions are put to the student
group, via LIHUFF/1, and from him to LIHUFF/2. This student group
happens to be one which will take direct and even physical actions
against communists.

3. Specifically, this student group:

a. Caused the termination of a Chinese Communist Art Exhibit
at UNAM by their direct action,’ and this was done at Station request
as a result of a request of Chief LNPURE.

i”
i

b. Paraded on 23 October 1966 with a black coffin and
signs in front of the Soviet and Cuban Embassies in mourning over
Soviet mis-treatment of Hungary in commemoration of the Anniversary

of the Hungarian Uprising.

i: c. Put a full-page advertisement in “El Universal", on
10 November 1966, which Eiiegedly came from a Communist Party member.
This student group made a (false) carnet for a student group member
with his photograph on it, and convinced this highly reputable

Chief of Station, Mexico City

1. On 24 October 1966, the Mexico City News, English language
daily, reported that approximately 200 students and members of the
Movimiento Universitario de Renovadora Orientacion (MURO), extreme
right wing organization, had gathered in front of the Soviet Embassy
on Sunday, 23 October, to commemorate the 10th anniversary of the
crushing of the Hungarian rebellion. The demonstration was broken
up by police but not before the students had placed a casket at the
entrance to the Soviet Embassy, and covered the sidewalk area with
banners and wreaths protesting the Soviet action in Hungary.

2. Some of the students formed another group and marched
to the Cuban Embassy wher: the police took into custody some 36 of.
the marchers. They were taken to the police headquarters, given a
lecture on the requirement for a permit to make such a "march" and
released. Among those arrested was Fernando Bajos Urquijo, Presiden
of MURO. No students were held by the police.

te

3. LIHUFF/1 advised COS, Mexico City, on 26 October 1966,
that he and LIHUFF/2 had planned the "march" and were very proud .
of their success and the publicity resulting from it. tere)

4. Enclosed are copies of press clippings from local daily

Objetivos de politica econémica de los grandes
paises industriales

Mo permitiré comenzar con algunas observaciones sobre
los objetivos de la politien econémica de los principales pafses
industriales del mundo libre, antes de tratar acerca do lox ing
trumentos que considero adeeuados ¥ legitimos para el lopro
de aquellos fines. Si no me equivoco, el objetivo de todos los
paises libres y regidos por la ley es Ja disminucién de la po-
breza, de la miseria y de las penalidades del mayor nimero
posible de sus ciudadanos y el aumento general de oportuni-
dades a fin de que todos los ciudadanos responsables y dignos
de ese nombre desarrollen ga propia personalidad. Este ohje-
tivo implica Ja obligaciin de respetar la dignidad y la integri-
dad dv todos los hombres de buena voluntad, Si se acepta es-
te chjetivo nacional la econom{a debe tener el cuadro institu-
cional capaz de promover una mejora progresiva del ingreso
real de los pueblos, mediante et mejoramicnto do ta producti-
vidad de los recursos humanos, naturales ¢ instrumentales.
Esto requiere, por lo que se refiere a la produectén de blenes
y servicios, una mayor divisién del trabajo y especializacién,
una creeiente eficacia cn Ia investigacién, mis espiritu de
inno my una mejor administracién de las empresas. Para
poder orientar esa tarca es esencial atribuir al consumidor el
poder soberano de decidir sobre In distribucién de los recur-
80s destinados a satisfacer sus necesidades y sus deseos, que
son cada vez més complejos y refinados, De esta forma se crea
un poderoso incentivo para que todo el mundo realice el esfuer-
Zo necesario para ganar e} dinero que requiere para obtener
Jos bienes que desea. El funcionamiento de este sistema se
garantiza de manera ideal en un mereado donde Jos precios se
mueven libremente gracias al plehiscite de tous le jours, y en
ef cual Ins amas do ensa y, en general, los consumidores, exe
Presin aus preferenciag on francos y céntimos, .o en délares
y¥ centavos. En Ia economia moderna, on Ja cunt esta forma
de distribucién de los recursos se aplica a todos los bienes,
duraderos 0 no, desde casas hasta los automéviles, y a todos
los servicios —educativos, médicos, culinarios, artisticos, re-
creativos, turisticos, de seguros, ete. cte.— el crecimiento eco-
némico tiende inevitablemente 2 ncelerarso y propagarse. Pa-
ra que tal crecimiento dindmico sea estable y continuo se re-

de Jos ingresos en los paises rurales del mundo, las que ocu-

Desde que estas grandes ideas han sido ensayadas durante
casi cuarenta afios en un experimento de laboratorio con va-
rios centenares de millones de personas, han perdido su brillo
y su atrayente colorido.

nusmo el mantenimiento de la convivencia pacifica entre las
naciones. Los paises industrinles necesitan una corriente ade
cuada y creciente de productos primarios de los pafses en vias
de desarollo, y pagarin por ellos, al igual que por los articu-

Una nueva concepcién del intercambio internacional:
el efecto Prebisch

A fin de comprender la situacién ambigua y confusa que
predomina actualmente en las capitales de las naciones indus-
trializadas de Occidente, trataré de esbozar a grandes Iineas

algunas do las ideas que dominaron las discusiones de la Con- -

ferencia de Ginebra. Los representantes de muchos paises
en desarrollo aceptaron como una nueva especie de ley natu-
ral inmutable cl Hamado “efecto Prebisch”, que atribuye la
debilidad de las balanzas de pagos de los paises exportadores
de productos primarios al deterioro de los términos de inter-
cambio. Desde esta perspectiva, los remedios aconsejables
serfan los siguientes:

_ Lies paises en desarrollo deben industrializarse con to-
da rapidez. Para lograrlo, deben abandonar el principio de Jas
ventajas comparativas y aceptar, como precio de Ia industria-
lizacién, costos superiores, en vez de inferiores, de los pro-

ile

cca TES TNR! MTNA TRI get prom mnt SEAS in”



ductos industriales, En consecuencia, deben proteger sus in-
dustrias; dicha proteccién puode Ievarse a cabo mediante
aranceles aduancros, impuestos 4 Ia importacién o cualquier
otro medio. Con el propdsito de fortalecer dicho proteccio-
nism, los pafses en vias de desarrollo deben agruparse y coris-
tituir uniones aduaneras con aranceles exteriores comunes
clevados.

2. Simultdneamente, los pafses industriales deben conce-
der trato preferencial para la entrada de exportaciones de
productos primarios de los paises en desarrollo a precios “ade-
cuados”, es decir, a precios remuncradores para los exporta-
dores,

3. A fin de impedir que los precios de los productos pri-
marios caigun por debajo de un minimun conyenido, los paf-
des en desarrollo deben imponer impuestos de cuantia varia-
ble sobre In exportaciin de las materias primarias, proporcio-
nales, en caso necesario, a una escala previamente fijada.

4. Todos los pafses deben estabilizar los precios de las
materins primas a un nivel beneficioso para los pafses expor-
tadores mediante convenios internacionales sobre mercancias,
asf como constituir reservas amortiguadoras y asignar cuo-
tas de-exportacién a tos pafses en vias de desarrollo.

5. Los paises. industriales deben suministrar una corrien-
te sustancialmenle mayor de eapitales a los paises en desa-
rrollo.

Mucho se puede afiadir o suprimir a este atrevido proyec-
to de reorganizacién total de la actual estructura institucional
del comercio internacional y del financiamiento para el des-
arrollo. Pero si las naciones industriales aceptaran, aunque
solo fuera parcialmente, Ja filosofia que impregna este pro-
yecto, la consecuencia seria la i:-uvitable paralizacién de una

considerable de ias fuerzas que otorgan a las economias
de Jos pafses industrinlizados y de una serie de pafses en de-
sarrollo, basadas en las decisiones descentralizadas de la eco-
nomfa, de mecado, su enorme dinamismo y su poderosa elas-
ticidad.

comtin: Suponen que la instituciin a escala mundial de un

¢la mundiel, La produccién de una tonelada de abono nitro-

Lo mis grave de toda intervencién conalatente en una
Tijacién de precios es que si bien, en principio, afecta a un
solo producto o a unos pocos productos estrechamente relacio-
nados, en realidad altera inevitablemente lug relaciones entre i
el precio de In. mercancia regulada y el precio de todas lags
restantes mercaneias y servicios. La insercion de un precio
rigido en una serie de precios flexilles de uncs 160 6 170
prodetos agricolas es algo asi como la conducta de un nifio
que, sin entender nada de lo que significa su actuacién, mo-
viese las palancas de un tablero de mando en una fabrica au-
tomatizada, Son imprevisibles todos los ajustes de largo al.
cance que deben efectuar lus agricultores y las demas partes
afectadas en respuesta a lag alleraciones en las relaciones
de precios causados por la fijacién de precivg de una sola
mercancia. Por ello, el expresado tratamiento aislado del me-
canismo de los precios en un solo pafs dard lugar a una mayor
incertidumbre en el futuro de la que suponia la inestabilidad
existente antes de Ian fijactin de precios, El argumento con
que xe defienden remedios como estos, que tlenen Ia virtud
de multiplicar los problemas, consiste en afirmur que el ajus- :
te de la oferta y la demanda no funciona bajo un régimen :
de precios flexibles, afirmacién que contradice integramente
la realidad y la experiencia econdmica,

El propésito de la estabilizacién se logra mientras la es-
tabilizacién tiende hacia el alza. Sin embargo, cuando se han
acumulado grandes existencias cuya distribucién es inevita-
ble, se producen las mismas consecuencias que cuando se sub-

1, The attached material relating to the establishment of "public awareness"
officials in U.S. businesses in Latin America was passed to COS by
LIHUFF-1, As can be seen from the correspondence between LIHUFF-1

and Mr, Smithies of the Council for Latin America Inc. regarding this
matter, the Council will attempt to interest U.S, parent companies in this
program, According to LIHUFF-1, the Council will also approach
Undersecretary of State Thomas Mann and his assistant, Robert Adame,

in line with LIHUFF-I's suggestion in his letter of 26 July 1965.

2, The attached correspondence and related material is being forwarded
with the request that it be passed to Robert Adams in anticipation of an
approach to his office by the Goancil for Latin America along the above

Mr, Al Wichtrich, Executive Vice President of the
American Chamber of Commerce in Mexico City, has given the
attached material to Win Scott for delivery to Mr. Adams in
anticipation of an approach to be made to Mr, Adams’ office
by the Council for Latin America, Inc., of New York re-
garding the establishment of “public awareness" officials
in U.S, business firms in Latin America, According to Mr.
Wichtrich, the Council for Latin America also intends to
appreach Under Secretary Mann for support in launching this

program.

OMLY QUALIFIED DESK,

Chief of Station, Mexico City.
THUFF

1. Ina letter to LIHUFF/1 dated 16 June 1965, LIHUFF/2 reported the
following:

The Escuela Nacional de Economia of the Universidad Nacional Autonoma
de Mexico (UNAM) has organized a program of summer courses in which
various Mexican and foreign professors have been invited to participate.
According to a circular issued by the UNAM, the following program of
courses was planned: 14 June: Prof. Michal Kalacki, Professor of the
Central School of Planning and Statistics in Warsaw, on the subj:ct
"Financing Economic Development in Mixed Economies." 15 June: Prof.
Joan Robinson of the University of Cambridge, England, on "The New Wave
in the Science of Economics." 16 June: Professor Arthur Smithies of
Harvard University, on "The Structured Polemic." 18 June: Prof.

Arthur Smithies, on a subject to be determined. 18 June: Round table
discussion with the following professors participating: Joan Robinson,
Michal Kalacki, Arthur Smithies, Horacio Flores de la Pefia, Jose Luis
Cecefia, Alonso Aguilar, Efigenia M. de Navarrete and Josue Saenz.

2, The above was reported by LIHUFF/1 to COS on 18 June. Station
information on the local Comnunist contacts of Joan Robinson has been
reported separately to COS, London and Headquarters.

Llowe, FD, [Atk
or
Willard C. CURTIS

1 Specific - LIHUFF Progress Report for February through March 1965
"ACTION REQUIRED - REFERENCES

XX_ J acrort_

1, The major occurrence during this period has been the reorganization of the
LIMUFP student organization. An entirely new board of directors was placed
at the head of the organization in’ March, The names of the old and new '
board of directorsQ¥: indicated in the neve item forvarded ag Separate Cover
Attachment No, 1. In addition thereto, as will be noted below, the +
board of directors of the LIHUFF student organization was reorganized at the
University of Puebla during thia period.

2, Other major activities during this period have been the following:

a, The LIHUFF student organization put out enother issue of its student

publication, copy of which is forwarded as Separate Cover Attachment No. 2.
LIBUFF/2 reported that 1000 copies of this publication were sold in a single
morning in the UNAM School of Law.

b. The new board of directors of the LIHUFF student group at the University
of Puebla was installed on 25 March. This was part of a reorganization under-
taken et that university due to che fact that the latter has continued to
slip further and further into the hands of far leftists. LIHUFF/2 noted

that the particular danger at this university is in the two faculties of
economy and philosophy since they are drawing Communist-oriented professors
from UNAM whose study programs and plans are drawn up accordingly. LINUFF/2
also indicated that with the situation as it is in Puebla there will be a
need for greater economic assistance there,

During this period, LIGUFF/2 reported that members of the LIHUFF student
organization had had to endure various types of harrassment from the far
leftist professors at UNAM, particularly in meeting academic requirecents..
Their organization was even accused cf being responsible for & beating!
thet one UNAM student suffered under cysterious circumstances, but; ‘siace
there was no involvemeat on the part of the LIHUFF group, the matter vas
soca dropped, "Crucero", # Christian Dezecratic publication, however,
continues to attack the LIHUFF students 25 being Ku-Klux-Klan types, In
order to combat this type of attack plus the charge of being a "secret"
organization, the LIWUFF students have been making a strong, conscious: effort
to have all their actions (such as e aew directorate) be accompanied, uit one
newspaper publicity and to do everything quite openly. One factor, though,
is being kept rather quiet: Sefiorita Cristina Borja, niece of Presideat
Gustavo Diaz Ordaz (probably. che daughter of a brother of Hrs, Diaz Ordaz
Whose maiden name was Borja), has become a menber of the LIBUPF student. --~° —,
organization, This, of course, is being handled in this canner due to the ~
domestic political considerations confronting the President, Separate Cover
Attachment No. 3 is a copy of an attack on the LIMUFF student jgroup carried
in the pro-Marxist "Siempre" issue of 17 Februery 1965, ; |; 75.

On 17 March, Identity 1 discussed With the COS LIHUFF/2 activities. Identity}
seid that, for years, his organization had been giving LINUFF/2 $20,000 (uN) Lae
annually for furtherance of his activities. Identity 1 asked if the COS
knew LINUFF/2 or anything about what he was doing. COS, of course, said that,
while he did not know LIHUFF/2 personally, he didinow that he had an economics ,
magazine and several other publications as well as an Institute.-. Since :
Identity 1 was obviously leading up to the point of whether; or not this
donation was going to a worthwhile cause, the COS said thatjhe thought, all: :
things considered, this was a good investment. Identity 1 then said that he ~
thought his organization would continue this subsidy in the’ same amount ‘to
LINUFF/2. wo ese

Olmos o menudo que reforma agraria es vital
en Latino América, pero en Venczuela seria més
exacto decir que el problema cs encontrar gente
deseosa de desarrollar y cultivar Ins vustas droas
No utillzadas que estén accesibles,

EI ais es mayor que Texas y Oklahoma jun-
tos, y tiene la poblacién de solamente siete y me-
dio millones, Gran parte del rea cultivable es
del gobierno, y el problema no es el de apaciguar
el hambre que la gente tiene de Posecr tlerras
sino mas bien, el de encontrar hombres y muje+
res dispuestos a ser Ploneros y habilitar nuevas
reas.

La experiencia venezoiana rudamente explota
la teoria Norte Americana de que se puede hacer
ala gente mas estable Pollticamente sachndolos
de los arrabales y dindoles buena casa,

Para la sorpresa det goblerno, so ha descu-
bierto que los alborotaderos del comunismo en
Caracas, no son Ins miserables barracas de los
Invasores de tierras en los alrededores de la ciu-
dad, sino mas bien los impresionantes aparta-
mentos que et goblerno construyé para proveer
de vivienda barata ¥ decente a los invasores de
derras,

El presidente de Venezuela es Rémulo Betan-
court, un hombre a quien en algunos cireulos se

tas y el terrorismo y criminalidad le representan
problemas crecientes. Tanto el terrorismo como
algunas de las reformas, han Preocupado a in-
versionistas en Venezuela, y en los ditimos afios
ha habido una desacoleracién en Ja tasa de cre-
cimiento econémico. Sospecho que el presidente

Comencé esta discusién haciendo ver que el
caso de Venczucla sugicre que el crecimiento eco-

ta aparente inconsistencia. :

Que estoy en favor del desarrollo econdmico,
defintivamente. Desco ver la miscria erradica-
da: no porque convenga a nuestros intereses po-
Uticos, sino porque conviene a los intereses de
las gentes de Latino América. Estoy también oa
favor de la justicla soctal por la misma razin.
Sin embargo, uno de los problemas bAsicos exis-
tentes es que los conceptos populares de justicia
social frecuentemente estin refiidos con aigu-
nos de los principios basicos de cconomia. Un
pals pucde tener impresionante crecimiento —
como Venezuela ha tenido— y adn sufrir de in-
estabjlidad politica, porque un sector sustancial
de Ja poblacién cree que la organizacién politica

¥, econémica de la sociedad es injusta. Por otio
ado, si los gobiernos sucumben a los conceptos

populurea de justicia socinl que son ecandnica-

no es probable tampoco que se logre estabilidad
politica, Me temo que atin no hemos dominudo

Esto sugiere que el problema Latino Ameri-

tuinosas.

Creo que a lo que todo esto Hleva, es que ol
dlagnéstico adecuado para Latino América no es

de ingresos. M4s bien, es una combinacién de

do y sufriendo no sélo Incomodidades persona-
les, sino atin arricsgando la vido para labrar un
mejor futuro para cellos y sus familias, mediante
su propio sudor y sacrificio.

Lo que me preocupa es quc nosotros realmen-

Una Politica Anacrénica Que Hunde Al Pais
ae Por PEDRO BELTRAN. |

N. del D.—Presentamos un articulo de Dn. Pedro Beltran, Ex Primer Ministro del
Peri, Presidente de la Sociedad Interamericana de Prensa y Director del diario Hy
“La Prensa” de Lima, Peri. El contenido de dieho .articulo puede ser perfectas |
mente aplicado @ nuestro pais. oe, !

No se puede Nevar a enbo una politica econémica verdadcramente moderna, audaz y progre-
sista (sin comillas) para procurar el bienestar de los peruanos, mientras no se abandonen ciertas
ideas que, ademas de demagdgicas —lo cual es en si mismo malo—, resultan anacrénicas —lo
sual es mucho peor. :

Alguien ha sefialado que, muy a menudo, las ideas que se imponen en el Peri como “revs
iueionarias”, como si fueran la dltima palabra en literatura, arte, ciencias sociales. 0 politica. ite-
gan a nuestras playas con un atraso de por lo mexios treinta o ctarenta aiios, es decir, cuanco
han sido superadas o cescartadas en sus paiscs de origen. Quien dijo eso se quedd corto en mix
teria de economia, pues las teorias econdmicas que estan “de moda” ahora en el Perd son ce co-
mienzos de siglo. Antes de la primera guerra mundial no se acertaba a pensar en otra mia
de mejorar la situacién de los trabajadores que no fuera quitar a los que mas tienen pari w:
‘a los mas necesitados. Y asi fue cobrando cuerpo la creencia en que el Estado deberia seguir

ea politica.
Inclusive los que no crefan en la modatidad comunista del despojo de la propiedad pe:
wserza, pensaton que se podia hacer lo mismo, poco a poco y pacificamenite, mediante impuestce
cada vez mas elevados; impucstos que distribuirian mejor la riqueza hasta igualar finalmeate «
codos los ciudadangs. 5

Aun sin considerar que, por este método, el Estado se queda con la mayor parte —cu- a
és— de lo que se “distribuye”, es evidente que con empobrecer a los ricos no se lograri:. envi
jecer a los pobres. Henry Ford, el famoso forjador de la gran industria automovilistica de los
Ystados Unidos, demostré tal cosa a un personaje pobre, no trabajador pero si amargado, que fue
_ yeprocharle la desigualdad entre sus respectivas fortunas y a exigirle que “compartiera su rk
“aeza” con todos. Ford le respondi i i
Je norteamericanos. Tome el délar que le toca, y déjeme en paz”.

vor de mis y mas impuestos, fabricaba toda clase de slogans que se esterotiparon y se convirtie-

1

gos proclaman la “emecién social” que los mueve! Como la Iglesia una y otra vez ha recordaio

Porque, gen qué consiste la verdadera:emocicn social, sin comillas? En el deseo sincero de
mejorar Ja condicion del hanibriento, del desccupado, del eniermo, ael favelo, del mal vestidy,

Propia buena ropa, los analiabetos se eduquen y 103 habitantes de tugurios vivan en casas uecentes:

La “emocién y 1a justicia sociales” falsas, con comillas, no consiguen siquicra mejorar a los

Se trata por cierto, de un ejemplo extremo, Pero indica una tendencia inevitable’de las me-
didas demagogicas, y concretamente de la demagogia tributaria: cuanto mas altos ¥ excesivos sean

gos al que ticne éxito, i

La demagogia, si logra su objetivo declarado de “igualar econémicamente” a los hombres,
Jo consigue por lo bajo, y cada vez mis bajo, reduciendo el nivel de vida de todos. La politica
econémica de bienestar —con premios para el riesgo, el esfuerzo y el éxito— eleva a todos, y mis
a Tos que menos tienen, y asi consigue atenuar las diferencias sin sacrificar la excelencia,” +

Por H. L. Richardson.

Cerea del Istmo de Ia ‘Trivialidad, en el Mar de la ‘patia, la nave‘de la Patria se und
lenta e Anexorablemente en el olvido, p : -

A bordé, la mayoria de los pasajeros y de la tripulacién estaban acostades al sol como
de eastumbre. Sobre la probabilidad inmedista de ahogarse, habla varios grados de eontiescis.
También habia dos érdenes de pensamientos sobre la materia, Un pequeiio grupo insistia no sm:
lamente en que si se bundia Ia nave, en realidad, esto era malo. Otro pequefio grupo inistfa en’
que era perfectamente eorrecto que se hundiera Ia nave, y es més, en que los pasajeros progre-
sistas, comunistas, socialistas, que miraban hacia el futuro, debfan ayudar a que esto sucediera
Las olas que sumergian la nave eran simplemente “las olas del futuro. ..”,

Miembros de este Gitimo grupo estaban callada pero sistemSticamente taladrando aguje-_
ros en el fondo del bareo para apresurar y asegurar el hundimiento de! mismo; alrededor de este
grupo de conspiradores estaba un grupo mucho més grande y ruidoso que defendia con sofis-
mas y falasias, Jos actos de estos que taladraban desde adentro. Sus explicaciones més comuncs
eran que:

~ " Primero—Los conspiradores no astaban realmente dafiando el barco sino aumentando su _

“seguridad porque los agujeros taladrados eran para permitir que el agua que ya estaba dentro |

de la nave fluyera hacia fuera; y |

Segundo.—z Qué importa después de a TAl fin y al cabo na shogadita nunca Je
hizo dafio a nadiel...*

En la proa del barco otro grupo pequefio elevaba sus oraciones, pldiendo la intervencién |
diving... un, esfuerzo lable Pero precisamente entre ellos, uno de los conspiradores taladraba
astduamente, y el grupo de fieles no hacia nada para impedirlo,



cos. Ellas se ccupatan de cuahdo en cuando con debares acaioradcs aceras de ia po: 3
clolégica y la sabiduria econémica de taladrar agujeros en el fondo del bareo, Finalmente cada
discusién terminaba con un acuerdo general que este procedimiento carecia de bases sélidas, y
el grupo acordaba firmar una resolucién en ese sentido para que fuera publieada en el periddico
del barco, Entre din.wr:éa y discusiin se ocupaban de otros asuntos académicos de importancia,
tales ‘como la historia de la perforacién de agujeros en las armadas del pasado.

Soure los mastiles estaba encaramado ofr» grupo numeroso de personas que trataba de
ignorarlo todo, Todos ellos esperaban que un viento politico empujara al barco hacia la playa

antes de que se hundiera, Desgraciadamente todos los vientos politicos soplaban hacia altamar

y no habia tierra a la vista, see a

~ La mayoria de les oficiales del barco estaban muy ocupados escribiendo y entregando to
tas a los conspiradores, ofreciéndoles taladros ms grandes, para que hicieran agujeros mas gran
des, para ‘que pudieran: sacar toda esa agua desagradable del barco con la mayor rapidez,

En el centro del barco habia un grupo pequeiio de pasajeros que dirigia el Capitin, de-
dicados a la tarea de impedir el hundimiento. Algugos de este grupo se esforzaban en hacer fun-
cionar las borabas. Otros trataban de tapar los agujecros Jo; mas ripido posible y en esta ope
racién recibian tremendas embarradas de lodo y mugre, Otros frataban de aprehender a los cons.
piradores para meterlos en la cArcel del bareo,’ pero sus esfuerzos se velan obstaculizados por su
escaso niimero, y por los cuerpos de la gente dormida, sobre los cuales tenfan que pasar. De vez
en cuando alguno de estos pasajercs dormidos habria un ojo y decia: “Sé que ‘deberia —
Pero no me gustan sus métodos”.

“En otra Grea protegida ¥ confortable, habe otro grupo, éste, una aglneracién de tebri-
4

E] espect4culo m4s curioso y a la vez mds patético lo presentaban sin embargo, unas per-
sonas que ya sabian que el barco se hurdia, que. ya estaban en la mar, y que apenas alcanzaban
8 gritar entre las ‘marejadas: “;Puedo luchar mejor independientemente!” a

El nuevo gobierno de la Repibliea ha promulgado como su meta la PLENA VIGENCIA de!
la Constitucién Mexieana y ha hecho un paneginco de la Libertad. i

La Constitucién Mexicana tiene un dia sefialado en el calendario para celebrar su promul-
gacién. Fue un verdadero acontecimiento registrado ya para siempre en los anales de nuestra
historia.

Desde el punto de vista politico, la Constitucién establecié tres poderes: Ejecutivo, Legislati-
vo y Judicial. Ello tenia por fin que la separacién de dichos tres poderes garantizara el bienestar °
social e individual, j
Desde el punto de vista econdmico, Ia Constitucién en su Articulo 28 establecé el sistema de
econémica, :
1

MECANISMO DE LA LIBERTAD ECONOMICA

guna clase; NI EXENCION DE IMPUESTOS; ni prohibiciones a titulo de proteccién a la indus- *
tria...” i!

la anes de violar este articulo Constitucional. 7

DERECHO DE PROPIEDAD

Pero todo lo anterior no tendria sentido, si el derecho de propiedad no estuviera también
garantizado,

Por edo la Constitucién garantiza el derecho de propiedad en su articulo 14 cuando dice:

SNADIE PODRA SER PRIVADO DE.LA VIDA, DE LA LIBERTAD 0 Dz SUS PROPIE.
PADES, POSESIONES 0 DERECHOS, sino mediante juicio sopuido ante ioe Triborane ar oe oe

las leyes expedidas con anterioridad al hecho’.

NADIE PUEDE SER MOLESTADO EN SU PERSONA, FAMILIA, DOMICILIO, PAPE-

de y motive ia causa legal del procedimiento”, - J“

muchos ataques.

¥ la falta de libertad en materia econémica es un atentado contra la propia libertad individual,

terrenos de propiedad privada rendian en forma. tan grande que alcanzaban el 35% de la produccidn
agricola en total, y el 50% de Ia produceién total de productos ganaderos. ‘

AVISO IRIPORTANTE

Hemos recibido en el Instituto un limitado donativo para emplearse en la difusién
de libros de gran interés socioeconémico. Dicho donativo se empleara en facilitar 2 pers
sonas como, macstros, estudiantes, profesionistas e interesados en materias socio-econe-
mnicas, la adquisicion del libro “Libertad y Abundi: ns del Lic. Gustavo R. Velasco, en
el cual se discuten muchos de los problemas econémicos de mayor actualidad en México,
Por ello, siendo el precio de dicho libro de $ 25.00 (MLN) en las librerias, el Instituto
le enviar a toda persona que envie la cantidad de $ 15.00 (M.N.) en cheque o giro Pos.
tal al Instituto, para tal objeto.

Este ofrecimiento se sostendri mientras no se agote el donativa que hemos reci-

bido,

En caso de que este primer proyecto tenga éxito, tenemos la seguridad de que
obtendremos otro donativo de alguna Persona que estime nuestra labor, para ofrecer
interesantes,

Communist Penetration of Mexican Catholic Activities

‘ACTON PEWURED REFINES,

Enclosed are reports that originated with the
Artime group of anti-Castro Cubans allegedly pertaining
to Communist infiltration into various segments of the
Catholic church in Mexico. In view of the references
to certain assets connected with Station operations,
the reports are forwarded for Station's information
and disposal,

Enclosures
Reports, h.w. Chester D, DAINOLD

Distribution:
Orig & 1 - COS, Mexico City

POR VICTOR RICO GALAN

El Arzobispo Primado de Méx-
co, Monsefior Miguel Dario Mi-
Tanda, dirigié a los fieles telacio-

nados con Ia educacién una car

Universitario de Renovaaora
Orientacién, enrevesado nombre
que tiene por objeto formar con
sus iniciales la palabra MURO.
Desde hace tiempo, el MURO ha
venido actuando en les medios estudiantiles en una forma
que sélo puede ser calificada de canallesca. Su principal
actividad aparente es la delacién, que usa para extorsio-

nar a todos aquellos que no se le someten. Se supone que
cuantos son ajenos a las actividades extremamente secia-
rias de] MURO, son comunistas, y como tales se les exhibe
en la picota.

Por otra parte, el MURO ejerce la violencia contra
aquellos estudiantes que no lo apoyan. Hay que suponer
que a estas formas de extorsién que han. trascendido al
pablico, se suman otias menos conccidas, pero no menos
inmorales y delictuosas. De una organizacién que ha le-
gado al extremo de Hamar comunista al padre dominico
Tomés Allaz, puede esperarse todo. El Primado de Méxi-
co dice en su carta muy claramente que “se aparta de las
directrices de la Iglesia y aun a veces de la misma ley mo-
ral, que debe normar todas las acciones humanas para
que sean licitas y bendecidas por Dios”.

En realidad, el MURO es una organizacién tipicamen-
te fascista. Pretende imponer a todo trance una ideologia
cavernicola, y no retrocede. ante la extorsién ni la violen-
cia fisica para lograrlo. Nada tiene, en el fondo, de caté-
Tica ni de cristiana. Pero se cobija bajo el manto de la
teligién, porque la, Jeoiesa la mayoria de los mexicanos ¥

_ espera con eso obtener la popularidad que, por su propia
naturaleza, le est4 vededa. Un viejo truco. Un viejo y po
drido truco.

Traer a Dios a la pelea callejera, con la macana o la
cadena, es la peor injuria que se le puede hacer. Ningun
czistimo auténtico podria admitir semejante cosa, pero

POR ROBERTO BLANCO MOHENO

La noche anterior a mi salida de Chi-
huahua, cuando comentaba con Javier
Palacio el horror de aquella situacién, la
imposibilidad de dejar de ser “peripa-
tético” ante el vicio'y el crimen herma.
nados para robar a un pueblo, la dolo-
Yosa necesidad de desafinar con amargas
verdades cuando todo el periodisme na-
ciooal forma el coro de las alabanzas,
una voz querida me dijo, desde México:

—Llegd un telegrama del general
Cardenas.

jDios! No cabe duda de que en la
vida existen las compensaciones. Porque
tenia en las manos, todavia, el ol. mal-
dito de la prision en que se mueren to-
dos Jos dias Rios, Cardona y Rodriguez
F.; porque la cronica indignacién se me
hacla un poco doloroso ante Ie nice,
indeseriptible de aquelia buena gente, y
el valor sacrificado de los estudiantes,
yla mterminable soledad del yermo de
Chihvabua, donde no viven ni siquiera
Jagartijas. El nombre de Cardenas, egoistamente, me hace olvidar, por
un momento no mas, la rabia impotente que me muerde el alma. Se
me permitira —lo permitira usted, Pepe Pagés— decir que al escu-
char el texto de ese telegrama siento tas entrafias todas del alma
lavadas y hallo, en un camina 2 cada dia mas duro, nuevas fuerzas
hacidas directamente de Ia mano de ese hombre maravilloso que es
don Lazaro. Si don Lazaro se pincha un deda —lo digo con el mismo
derecho, y el mismo fervor, con que he dicho sobre él algunas inevi-
tables amargas verdades— de ese dedo no sale sangre... jsale Me.
xico!

Haria un mes que habia mandado un mensaje a Ciudad Alta:
mirano, uno de los centros vitales de la Comisién del . dicién-
dole a Cardenas que si era todavia oportuno, me gustaria conocer la
verdadera situacién de la zona guerrerense y michoacana afectada por
Jos recientes temblores para ver la manera de hacer Uegar al Presi-
dente Lépez Mateos, patio de todas las lagrimas, las necesidades que
les sefiores gobernadores tienen la costumbre de no ver, ciegos casi
todos a puro egoismo. Cuando pasaron las semanas y de Cindad AL.
tamirano nada llegé, sentf un poco de mordedura del despecho. Es
cierto que he dicho en estas paginas mi condena del a CCI y de sus
dirigentes comunistas —aunque no egé a insultarlos como los pro-
pios campesinos de esa Central hace unos dias, en que los echaron
ignominiosamente—; es verdad que acedi a dos Teuniones de los diri-
Bentes del Movimiento de Liberacién Nacional, entre los cuales desta-
caban Cuauhtémoe Cardenas, Alonso y Gonzilez Pedrero, y que me
Tetiré indignado ante la absurda Postura, la inmovilidad y hasta la
cobardia que encontré: y algo mas grave: tuve necesidad, en mi libre
“El Cardenismo”, de ahondar en algunas cosas que forzosamente do-
Heron al gran michoacano. Pero no queria, no podia creer que el
Expropiador del Petroleo, el padre agrarista, el campedn del Derecho
Internacional sufriera la mezquina enfermedad que padecen nuestres
intelectuales rojos. ;Si hay un hombre al que nunca debe Ilamarsele
intelectual, dado el giro que la palabrita ha tomado de quienes asi
se Maman, ese hombre es Cardenas! Y ahora escuchaba el texto
del_mensaje que muy poco después iba a revelarme la grandeza de
México y Ix miseria de México, toda la enorme y dolorosa paradoja
que es este formidable pais: “Recibi con enorme retraso tu mensaje
Porque no,esture aqui. Seris tienvenido cuando quieras’. No quic.
10, Pepe Pages, aumento de sueldo: jya estoy pagado lo suficiente!

*

Biauee Moneno

corazén de esta desolada region, de pobreza subhumana, sin recursos,
pues si bien es cierto que “no bay tierra mala con agua” aqui no, hay
tierra, sino tequesquite, piedra, tepetate, erosion, se levanta un ipue-
biito viejo en su anénimo dolor, en su hambze de siglos: se lathaba
Mariscala de Iturbide. Algo ha ganado, en un sentido moral, porque
a la fecha se Hama Mariscala de Juarez. Ei que escribe confiesal que
nunca habia oido hablar de este pueblo. Y junto al caserio misedable
veo desde el avién que conduce magistralmenie el capitan Rufino! Sal-
gado una magnifica pista de aterrizaje. Y distuingo, desde el pire,
luna figura roquefia, hecha de esta misma tierra pobre, que hace un
alto pequeno en su trabajo de siempre para corrermé una cortesia
mexicanisima, : 1
— Mira —digo a mi hijo Carlos a quien he traido porque considero
que ver trabajar a Cardenas entre el pucblo es la mas alia leccion
que puede recibir un joven— alli esta el genercl A sti edad, jnor-
diendo los setenta aiics, con su fama, su leyenda y su signification,
este hombre podria estar recosteda tranquilamente en el seno de 16
Historia. Podria tener negocios enormes y decscar sus horas al! pia.
cer ya lo intriga, dedicaciones ex-presidencssles por excelencia. Se
levanta a las cinco de ia majiana y suelen darie las doce de la noche
pepado al trabajo. Es preciso, muchacho, que comprendas el privile-
gio de que gozas. Estu tu visita tiene la misma significacion Gur si,
Por ua mulagro, estuvieras Uegando al campamento de José Marial Mo-
Telos 0 a la oficina errante de Benito Juarez es
Un abrazo y sin mas transicién los yips echan a andar rumBo al
blado, en una de cuyas casas esta iastaiada la oficina del Yocal
sjecutive. Mientras despacha algunos radios. pues aqui'no hay te
legrafo, y atiende a unos campesinos de un pueblo que en esta zona
al parecer maldita Heva el nombre absurdo de “La Inspiracion”. vo
charlo con los ingenieros Lastari, Residente de la zona; Valdes Al.
varez, Director de Comunicaciones y Urbanismo: Guillermo Soto, Sub-
director; Jaime Traslosheros, Obras Hidrdulicas, y Luis Suarez Fer-
nandez, encargado de investigaciones economicas. Estos ‘hombres,
eternos pioneros, duros trabajadores que construyen México z su
randeza, cuya misién terrible pero satisfactoria y’ bella ‘consisté en
irse de los lugares cuando los lugares se han hecho habitables v; tie.
nen ya caminos, y agua potable, y electricidad y. sobre todo, escuelas,
tienen la vena jocunda y Ia paciencia larga. Liegaron aqui cuando la
Alta Mixteca no era sino una enorme tragedia sin caminos, ni luz, ni
comida siquiera. Traian dinero en los bolsillos, pero pasaban hambre,
que en esta region, donde miles y miles de mercanos viven 0%
ven?— en la mds terrible miseria, los frijoles, icase. bien, los friples
son un lujo. Nadie conoce aqui la leche y cuando recogen un hijevo
de la gallina ranchera que algunos “ricos” tienen..ese huevo n§ es
comido por ellos, sino que sirve de moneda suprema para el: inter-
cambio de pequefias mercancias. snag
Y sin embargo, frente a esta miseria, no he sentido ni por un
momento la indignacién. la rebeldia que me mordié ef Chihuahua,
porque lo terrible —con serlo— no es que una zona sea! miserable.
aunque desde luego el hombre tiene la obligacién de luchar cobra:
lo que los sefiores curas.dé-la region Haman “la voluntad dp Dis”,
sino que donde hay riquezas, como en Chihuahua, la traicién, 'el rébo,
el crimen, presiden todas las cosas. Aqui se lucha por ayudar all in-
feliz mixteco, que a pesar de tener hambre de sizlos —los ‘ingeni
me han dicho que pesos que en otras regiones son movidos facilmante
yr dos hombres aqui requieren seis— es un indio vivaz en cuyas
comunidades el alcoholismo crénico —la verdadera enfermedad | in-
digena, una enfermedad inoculada por los traficantes mestizos y blan-
no alcanza las proporciones espantables de Chiapas 0 Yucatan.

the Communist threat; ami it has accumulated a file of basic data cn event and : 4
individuals revolving about Communiem and Socialism that would be difficult for
any private Mexican group to duplicate. ,‘This is quite aside from the many :
individuals, such as LICHANT), who have gravitated to LIHUFF and present 5
various types of capabilities in the press, publishing, and similar fields.] 4
nace
b, LIHUFF and its sponsors are considered in terms of the Mexican i
scene as extreme right-wing conservatives; however, on the PBPRIME scene ‘
they would be considered more as cent.ists, The importance of such a group,
vocal and combative, existing in Mexico, is not in absdute terms but in relative
terms. As is known by Headquarters, the ruling Partido Revolucionario
Inetitucional (PRI) party is basically a delicate reflector of the many political
currents and pressures that exist in Mexico. In elections, appointments and
decisions, the PRI cabal weighs very carefully all political equities, If only the
extreme leftists are vocal and active, then the decisions tend to be weighted
in their favor and oriented toward their vewpoint, In so many words, in order (‘¢5-
to keep some kind df counterbalance, even though tending towards extremes, $
the right must be as vocal and active as the left, Essentially, thie is where
the Station sees the value of the LIHUFF mechanism, It does not expect Mexico
ever to revert to the LIHUFF philosophy or objectives en totoor even to any 5
very great degree; it does expect LIHUFF to exercise an influence and restraint |
on Mexico succumbing to the pressures and demands of the far left, Unless
some feW like LIHUFF/2 ‘aiid Miguel ALEMAN Valdes were active through :
organizations of their type, the political center of gravity would move further i
towards the far left unchecked and further than ODYOKE policy would care ‘> t
see it, This is the unique and specific value that this Station has seen, and {
continues to see, in the LIHUFF activity. {
ay :
¢. In mid-1960, on the strength of a UHUFF/2 contact with HBFINCH,
the Chief HBFINCH (Mexico) requested the Station to consider support of the
LIHUFF activity. A check with Headquarters indicated that KUBARK had been
Providing some support to LIHUFF through Identify 3, "But inasmuch as Identity 3
had died shortly before, the Station was asked by Headquarters to pick up the i
funding. The Station funding initially was directed to Identity’4, the major. H
regular publication of LIHUFF. A project was submitted by the Station in i
reference C, but reference D indicated the project had been disapproved in the
form submitted, that support to Idents#"+-should be discontinued, and that
instead, the Station funds should be applied to the student activity (Identity 2) #40}
on a spot assistance basis, This was dong with PBPRIME business associates
of LIHUFF/I picking up the cost of Identity“# some $1,200 (US) per month.
At the present time, therefore, Station expenditures are confined to LIHUFF/1
salary ($500 per month) and $500 per month to Identity,2~7At this juncture aad
, the LIHUFF activity is costing $12, 0v0 per year.

Station access to, and control of, this activity depends primarily on
the relationship of LIHUFF/1 with LINUFF/2. Precisely what percentage of

however, it is known that PBPRIME businees men are underwriting Identity 4
to the extent of $1200 (US) per month, The circulars and other activities
sustained by LIHUFF must involve, conservatively, another $1200 (US) per
month, The $500 (US) per month funded to LIHUFF by the Station, while i
maintaining access and certainly providing useful support to LIHUFF in the {
student field, cannot be considered control insurance in this situation,
Essentially, Station funds assure access for LIHUFF/I to LIHUFF/2 on LIHUF!
matters and, with this entree, LIHUFF,] on the strength of their personal j
relationship, provides the control factor. Basically, the control factor is Q
probably guaranteed more by the personal relationship than the funds, In any
event, the control over LIHUFF activities is not absolute and, even given
complete funding of LIHUFF by KUBARK, would not be absolute, Possibly,
it could be improved a little more with some more funds, but not much,

This is because LIHUFF/2 is successful, prominent, capable and invdved with ;
too many other prominent people and events on his own to ever have any single :
individual or entity dictate bis activities, attitudes, and soon, He is responsive
to Station requirements on the use of Station funds and even seeks advice on
other LIHUFF activities not funded by the Station, What he is not readily
responsive to is desailed written reportins: He will give oral reports and
some written reports, Part of the problem in this regard undoubtedly is that
he is involved in so many activities that he finds it difficult to find the time.
For Station purposes in this particular program, the control is less than ideal
but certainly adequate for getting things done in the areas desired since there
is little question about his motivation and ability.

are operating in UNAM, a university of upwards of 80,000 students,
Thos far, there has been no problem of conflict since one is working the

Catholic side of the street and the other, the so-called "independents" --and
there is still plenty of room for both to operate, In this connection, it should :
be noted that a great deal of LIHUFF student effort is devoted to several f

universities outside Mexico City; in other words, the UNAM is just one aspect.

b. LISIREN: This project is concerned with a mass propaganda
approach to Communism in Mexico, It is headed by a group of businessmen
The nly relationship between LINUFF and LISIREN is;
in the fact that four of the members of Identity o are members of LIHUFF's | +
twenty-six man "Bard of Director This does not necessarily mean an i :
interlocking directorate between the two projects as indicated in previous Heady =
quarters correspondence, since, as in many similar activities in the PBPRIME,
individuals interested in civic or outside activities of this nature are frequendy
tapped to serve in multiple assignments of this nature, At this juncture, with
LIHUFF concentrating on student activities in selected bigger universities, it
is nct believed that there is any particular relatimship of operational relevance
or import between these two instrumentalities, There are just four men
common to both boards.

saat ata

ae Leda,

c. LILISP/C: Since LILISP/C ie a national student organization,
stressing student affairs in the interior of Mexico, obviously LIHUFF and
LILISP/C are working in the same general field in nniversities outside Mexico |
City. However, in the particular universities in which LIHUFF is concentra
its efforts, this can be a complementary relationship since LIHUFF can work
much more depth in these universities taan can LILISP/C and can affiliate its |
groups to the LILISP/C national student confederation which 1s the only one now
generally recognized in Mexico. LILISP/C, as a national student confederation,
obviously can only spend very limited time on any single university or situation.

5. The Mexico City Station did not get involved in the P.N.M. activities |
of LIHUFF/Y, either directly or indirectly.

‘
6. The Movimiento Universitario Renovadora Orientacion (M.U.R.0.) groups 4
at the National University and at the Universities of Puebla, Morelia (Michoacan)
and Guadalajara continued their anti-Comminist campaigns. At the National
University (U.N.A.M.), in particular, M.U.R.0. vigorously supported the
Mexico Station's student candidates and organizations. This vas a result of
LIWUFF/1 guidance which he received from the Station.

on student activities, primarily concerning the U.N.A.M.

8. As an exemple of MU.R.O. anti-Communist activity the leaders of this
organization sent telegrams to Santiago, Chile and to the Chilean Enbassy in |
Mexico City protesting the (then plans for) holding of the Latin American Youth
Congress (Communist) in Chile. ‘vo of these leaders also visited the Chilean
Embassy in Mexico and pretended to be interested in visas to go to this Congress
and made remarks about this Communist Congress. a

III, PROBLEMS:

9. aun, View Of the lack of formalized status and dependence upon OOA funds!
for financing, the principal problem has been to find cleared businessmen
(Americans) to whom the Station could appeal for continued financial support of
the publication and some student activities of the LIEUFF groups.

|

Tv. PLANS:

10. The Station plens to abide by reference C insofar as expenditures from
Station funds are concerned. Any other financial support will of necessity have
to come from interested U.S. businessmen.

11. The Station plans to coutinue to use the M.U.R.O, student organization |
86 a vigorous and "shock troop" type group in support of Station and KUBARK
student anti-Commmist objectives. The M.U.R.0. group will also continue to
be used as sources of information of interest on University activities.

12, The Mexico City Station can also use LIHUFF/2 as e writer (who cen on bie
own get articles in "El Universal" and "Excelsior", Mexico's two biggest and best
nevspapers). His use will be restricted to strongly anti-Commnist, anti- i
Soviet articles.
V. SECURITY:

33. ‘There have been no security problens during this period. Only LIEUFF/1

is aware of ODYOKE involvement; LIRUFF/2 and others believe businessmen are
still the sources of fimds and guidances. ;

ik. As stated in paragraph 10 above, the Station plans henceforth to spend

“a.” $500 (dollars) monthly to support student activities, primarily |
¥U.R.0.5 and

b. $500 (dollars) monthly as the salary to LIHUFF/1.

15. . Any other monies LIHUFF gets as a result of Station actions will come a
from support of U.8, business contacts of the Station. :
